# crates

Parent: [[code/repo|Repository Overview]]

## Overview

The `crates` workspace groups the Gobby toolchain's component crates, each a standalone CLI/library with a focused role:

- **gcode** — A Postgres-backed code intelligence CLI and library for indexing, searching, and analyzing source code across many languages (graph, vector, and BM25 search; symbol resolution; codewiki generation).
- **gcore** — Shared foundational layer providing config resolution, service clients (Postgres, FalkorDB, Qdrant), AI routing, graph analytics, schema/setup, and secret handling consumed by the other crates.
- **ghook** — A hook-dispatch CLI bridging agent tooling (Claude, Codex, Droid, Gemini) to the gobby daemon, wrapping hook events in versioned envelopes and translating daemon responses into hook actions.
- **gloc** — A CLI that launches AI client binaries against configurable LLM backends (including local Ollama), resolving backends, clients, models, and environment from layered YAML config.
- **gsqz** — A configurable command-output compression tool that shrinks verbose shell output via regex-matched pipelines defined in YAML.
- **gwiki** — A scope-aware (global/project/topic) wiki and knowledge-base CLI built on a raw-first, immutable storage model, supporting ingestion, search, ask, research, compile, audit, and source management.

Together these crates form a cohesive code- and knowledge-intelligence platform sharing common service, configuration, and AI infrastructure through `gcore`.
[crates/gcode/assets/import_roots/elixir_dependency_roots.json:2]
[crates/gcode/assets/import_roots/ruby_require_roots.json:2]
[crates/gcode/contract/gcode.contract.json:2]
[crates/gcode/src/cli.rs:21-44]
[crates/gcode/src/cli/tests.rs:5-213]

## Child Modules

- [[code/modules/crates/gcode|crates/gcode]] - The `crates/gcode` module implements gcode, a Postgres-backed code intelligence CLI and library for indexing, searching, and analyzing source code across many languages.

It is organized into three parts:

- **src** — The implementation root containing the full toolchain: language-aware parsing and symbol/import/call extraction (with C++ clangd integration), file discovery and classification, multi-language import resolution, freshness and project-lock management, and identity/config/database bootstrapping. Search spans symbol, text, content (BM25), grep, and semantic/vector retrieval, alongside a FalkorDB-backed code graph supporting callers, usages, imports, blast-radius, lifecycle sync, and project graph reports. Higher-level features include hierarchical "codewiki" documentation generation (with AI prompting, citation grounding, and ownership/blame attribution), Qdrant vector lifecycle management, embeddings doctor diagnostics, standalone Postgres setup, and skill installation.

- **contract** — A single machine-readable JSON artifact (`gcode.contract.json`) defining the versioned CLI surface: global flags, per-command definitions, identity keys, JSON output keys, and error codes, serving as the source of truth for parsing, validation, and tooling integration.

- **assets** — Static JSON data cataloging well-known dependency and import roots (Elixir and Ruby) to help the indexer recognize standard-library and third-party package boundaries during import resolution, plus a bundled SKILL.md.

A core design principle, enforced by tests, is that the library API remains CLI-independent.
[crates/gcode/assets/import_roots/elixir_dependency_roots.json:2]
[crates/gcode/assets/import_roots/ruby_require_roots.json:2]
[crates/gcode/contract/gcode.contract.json:2]
[crates/gcode/src/cli.rs:21-44]
[crates/gcode/src/cli/tests.rs:5-213]
- [[code/modules/crates/gcore|crates/gcore]] - Module: crates/gcore

gcore is the foundational Rust crate for the Gobby stack, providing configuration, AI routing, persistence, and infrastructure provisioning shared across the workspace.

Key responsibilities:
- **AI transport & routing**: A transport-neutral client (`AiTransport`) for daemon and direct backends covering text generation, transcription, vision, and embeddings, with retry/backoff, rate-limit handling, capability probing, per-capability routing resolution, concurrency limiting (`AiLimiter`), and result/error types (`AiError`, `TextResult`, `TranscriptionResult`, `VisionResult`).
- **Configuration**: Layered config sources (env, YAML/standalone, Postgres config store) with secret resolution (Fernet decryption, env/secret expansion), capability bindings, and typed configs for FalkorDB, Qdrant, embeddings, and indexing. `CoreContext` and `AiContext` assemble resolved settings.
- **Persistence & search**: FalkorDB graph client with query escaping and graph analytics (centrality, communities, bridges, hotspots); Qdrant vector client with scoped collections and upsert/search; hybrid search primitives (RRF merge, BM25 scoring, query sanitization); Postgres connection helpers with TLS/sslmode handling and schema validation.
- **Infrastructure provisioning**: Docker Compose service provisioning (FalkorDB, Qdrant, PostgreSQL with custom pg_search/pgaudit image), hub identity resolution and conflict detection, daemon endpoint discovery, local backend detection/probing, project root/ID resolution, and content-hash-based incremental indexing.
- **Setup validation**: Runtime and attached validators reporting structured setup guidance and degradation diagnostics.

The crate emphasizes domain-neutral primitives (consumer-supplied graph names, collection scopes, and chunk metadata), redaction of sensitive database URLs, and extensive test coverage with fake transports and config sources. Containerized service assets ship alongside the source in `assets/`.
[crates/gcore/assets/docker-compose.services.yml:5-117]
[crates/gcore/assets/postgres-pgsearch/version.json:2]
[crates/gcore/src/ai/daemon.rs:19-24]
[crates/gcore/src/ai/mod.rs:30-34]
[crates/gcore/src/ai/probe.rs:20-23]
- [[code/modules/crates/ghook|crates/ghook]] - The `crates/ghook` crate provides ghook, the hook-dispatch CLI that bridges agent tooling (Claude, Codex, Droid, Gemini) to the gobby daemon. It detects the calling CLI and per-hook criticality (`CliConfig`), parses incoming hook payloads, optionally injects terminal/tmux context, and wraps events in versioned envelopes before dispatching them to the daemon over HTTP. Daemon responses are translated into hook actions—continue, JSON blocks, exit-two, or stderr passthrough—with failure handling that distinguishes critical from non-critical hooks and transport errors. Additional capabilities include offline inbox enqueue/quarantine with at-least-once delivery and cleanup, statusline forwarding to downstream commands, post-shutdown suppression via freshness markers, and a `diagnose` subcommand reporting CLI detection, daemon connectivity, terminal context, and install provenance.

The crate's structured outputs are governed by two JSON Schemas in `schemas/`: `diagnose-output.v2.schema.json` (diagnostic report format) and `inbox-envelope.v1.schema.json` (queued hook event envelopes with Gobby project/session headers), which serve as the validation and documentation source of truth. An extensive test suite validates envelope serialization, action mapping across all four CLIs, dispatch suppression logic, terminal-context capture, inbox delivery, and schema conformance.
[crates/ghook/schemas/diagnose-output.v2.schema.json:2]
[crates/ghook/schemas/inbox-envelope.v1.schema.json:2]
[crates/ghook/src/cli_config.rs:11-18]
[crates/ghook/src/detach.rs:23-43]
[crates/ghook/src/diagnose.rs:15-32]
- [[code/modules/crates/gloc|crates/gloc]] - The `gloc` crate is a CLI tool that launches AI client binaries (e.g. Claude, Codex) against configurable LLM backends, including local Ollama models. It loads layered configuration (built-in defaults plus YAML overrides in `config.yaml`) defining backends, clients, model aliases, and settings such as probe timeouts and auto-load/pull behavior. Core responsibilities include resolving the active backend, client, and model (with template and alias expansion), building environment variables and command arguments, locating the target binary, and execing the client process. It also probes backend reachability and ensures Ollama models are present and warmed up before launch. A `main` entry point and `Cli` parser drive subcommands like init, status reporting, and config export, backed by an extensive unit test suite.
[crates/gloc/config.yaml:11-17]
[crates/gloc/src/backend.rs:7-12]
[crates/gloc/src/config.rs:13-22]
[crates/gloc/src/exec.rs:9-21]
[crates/gloc/src/main.rs:16-52]
- [[code/modules/crates/gsqz|crates/gsqz]] - The `gsqz` crate is a configurable command-output compression tool that shrinks verbose shell output while preserving meaningful content. It is driven by a YAML configuration (`config.yaml`) defining global settings (minimum output length, max compressed lines, empty-output behavior), a set of command-matched pipelines, and a fallback path. Each pipeline matches commands via regex and applies an ordered sequence of compression steps.

The core engine (`src`) compiles pipelines and runs a `Compressor` that splits compound commands, applies built-in and configured exclusions, selects the matching pipeline by command basename, and produces a `CompressionResult` tracking savings percentage and passthrough status. Compression steps are modular: line filtering, mode-based grouping (git status/diff, pytest and generic test failures, lint-by-rule, by-extension/directory/file, errors/warnings), deduplication of near-identical lines, regex replacement, head/tail truncation (whole or per-section), early-exit `match_output` rules, and multi-level prose compression that protects code blocks, URLs, paths, and frontmatter.

A CLI front end supports both input and output modes, optional daemon-based config fetching, and savings reporting. The module ships a comprehensive test suite covering command splitting, exclusion logic, configuration loading/serialization, and every compression step.
[crates/gsqz/config.yaml:12-15]
[crates/gsqz/src/command_split.rs:5-85]
[crates/gsqz/src/compressor.rs:7-12]
[crates/gsqz/src/config.rs:26-35]
[crates/gsqz/src/daemon.rs:11-23]
- [[code/modules/crates/gwiki|crates/gwiki]] - gwiki is a scope-aware (global/project/topic) wiki and knowledge-base CLI built on a raw-first, immutable storage model. The `src` implementation root pairs a `main.rs`/`commands` CLI layer with a `contract.rs` flag specification and JSON/text output rendering, dispatching subcommands for setup, indexing, ingestion, search, ask, read, refresh, compile, research, review, audit, export, health, trust, librarian, lint, and source management.

Ingestion handles diverse media—URLs, local files, PDFs, Office documents, images, audio, video, git repositories, MediaWiki, and Wayback captures—with transcription, vision, and document-extraction clients that degrade gracefully when AI or media tooling is unavailable. Derived content is indexed into PostgreSQL (BM25 keyword search), Qdrant (semantic vectors), and FalkorDB (graph relationships), with fused multi-source retrieval, graph-boosted ranking, and provenance tracking. Higher-level workflows include AI-driven research loops, page synthesis/compilation, citation-quality and trust reporting, link analysis, and change-triggered refresh.

The accompanying `contract` module publishes a machine-readable `gwiki.contract.json` describing every command's flags, positionals, JSON output keys, dependency metadata, and degradation behavior, while `assets/skills` provides Markdown skill definitions (audit, compile, query, research) for guiding wiki operations.
[crates/gwiki/contract/gwiki.contract.json:2]
[crates/gwiki/src/ai/chunk.rs:20-26]
[crates/gwiki/src/ai/clients.rs:20-23]
[crates/gwiki/src/ai/translate.rs:6-29]
[crates/gwiki/src/api.rs:11-121]
